10.1016/j.jmp.2023.102819
No data was used for the research described in the article.

Knowledge space theory (KST) provides a useful and efficient mathematical psychological framework for assessing individuals’ knowledge and facilitating further learning ( Doignon & Falmagne, 1985 ). In KST, the knowledge of an individual is represented by his/her so-called knowledge state  
                         K 
                      , that is the set of all the items  
                         q 
                       in a knowledge domain  
                         Q 
                       he or she proved to master. The collection  
                         K 
                       of the states that can be observed in the population, which contains at least  
                         ∅ 
                       and the knowledge domain  
                         Q 
                      , is the knowledge structure ( Doignon & Falmagne, 1985; Falmagne et al., 2006 ). Knowledge states and knowledge structures are the fundamental concepts in KST, and the construction of these states and structures constitutes a critically important problem. Several methods exist for constructing knowledge structures, such as query-routine ( Koppen, 1994; Koppen & Doignon, 1990 ) and the ps-query routine ( Cosyn & Thiery, 2000 ), which are designed to build knowledge structures and knowledge states through interviews with experienced experts.  Schrepp (2003)  describes a method of explorative data analysis, which allows for the identification of logical implications between items in a dichotomous questionnaire or test. There exist also methodologies to extract skill maps from data collections ( Spoto et al., 2016 ). Additionally, an effective method to construct knowledge structures involves the analysis of item-skill relationships. Skill  
                         s 
                       represents a method, a strategy or an ability for a subject to solve a set of items. Given a domain  
                         S 
                       of skills, a particular subset  
                         T 
                       of  
                         S 
                       represents an individual’s mastery of skills ( Anselmi et al., 2017; Doignon, 1994; Falmagne et al., 1990; Heller et al., 2017, 2013 ). The skill assignment is represented by the so-called skill map, which depicts the relationship between items and skills. Skills in KST enable the analysis of behavior’s interpretation. However, for a given skill  
                         s 
                      , different items may require varying proficiency levels of  
                         s 
                       for successful resolution, and individuals may exhibit different proficiency in the same skill. All these factors can significantly influence the solution of items within the domain  
                         Q 
                      . Thus, it is natural to introduce the concept of fuzzy skill pairs  
                         
                            ( 
                            s 
                            , 
                            l 
                            ) 
                         
                      , where  
                         
                            l 
                            ∈ 
                            
                               [ 
                               0 
                               , 
                               1 
                               ] 
                            
                         
                       represents the proficiency level of skill  
                         s 
                      . Specifically, when skill proficiency is limited to only 0 or 1, fuzzy skills become classical skills. This implies that skills are special cases of fuzzy skills. Similar to skill maps, fuzzy skill assignments are represented by fuzzy skill maps ( Sun et al., 2021 ). Additionally, some knowledge structures can be delineated via conjunctive and disjunctive models by fuzzy skill maps.

Forward-graded (FG) structures and backward-graded (BG) structures have garnered significant attention in recent years ( Spoto & Stefanutti, 2020; Spoto et al., 2012 ). Moreover, any learning space ( Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 ) is FG in at least one item, while the complement of any learning space is a BG structure ( Spoto et al., 2013 ). Furthermore, Basic Local Independence Models (BLIM) applied to FG or BG structures are unidentifiable ( Heller, 2017; Spoto et al., 2012 ). Therefore, Forward-graded (FG) and backward-graded (BG) structures hold particular importance in KST. For a skill map  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            S 
                            , 
                            τ 
                            ) 
                         
                      , if a skill  
                         
                            s 
                            ∈ 
                            S 
                         
                       satisfies  
                         
                            s 
                            ∈ 
                            τ 
                            
                               ( 
                               q 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            s 
                            ∉ 
                            τ 
                            
                               ( 
                               p 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       for all  
                         
                            p 
                            ∈ 
                            Q 
                            ∖ 
                            
                               { 
                               q 
                               } 
                            
                         
                      ,  
                         s 
                       is called a specific skill for an item  
                         
                            q 
                            ∈ 
                            Q 
                         
                      . This type of skill is crucial in defining FG and BG knowledge structures ( Spoto et al., 2012 ).  Spoto and Stefanutti (2020)  established necessary and sufficient conditions for delineating FG and BG knowledge structures from skill maps.

Building upon some of the theoretical results in previous articles, we aim to establish the connection between FG (or BG) knowledge structures and fuzzy skill maps.  Spoto and Stefanutti (2020)  found that the closure space (respectively, knowledge space) delineated by the skill map is backward (respectively, forward) graded in an item  
                         
                            q 
                            ∈ 
                            Q 
                         
                       if and only if  
                         S 
                       contains a specific skill for  
                         q 
                      . This implies that the presence of certain specific skills indicates the forward-gradedness or backward-gradedness of the delineated knowledge structure in item  
                         q 
                      . However, the situation is different in fuzzy skill maps. Specific skills cannot be used in fuzzy skill maps. In place of specific skills, we incorporate specific upper and lower fuzzy skills, which are essential for delineating BG and FG knowledge structures through the use of fuzzy skill maps. We find that a fuzzy skill map with specific upper fuzzy skills in item  
                         q 
                       is a necessary and sufficient condition for having the BG simple closure space in  
                         q 
                      . At the same time, a fuzzy skill map with specific lower fuzzy skills in item  
                         q 
                       is a necessary and sufficient condition for having the FG knowledge space in  
                         q 
                      . In particular, when the proficiency of skills takes value only in 0 or 1, specific skills in skill maps are both specific upper and lower fuzzy skills in fuzzy skill maps. In this way, it can be seen that  Theorem 1  in  Spoto and Stefanutti (2020)  is a special case of  Theorem 1  and  Theorem 2  in our paper. On the other hand,  Spoto and Stefanutti (2020)  established the necessary and sufficient conditions for forward-graded closure spaces and backward-graded knowledge spaces. However, in fuzzy skill maps, for the similar conditions of  Theorem 2  in  Spoto and Stefanutti (2020) , we find only conjunctive models can delineate forward-graded closure spaces, while disjunctive models do not necessarily delineate backward-graded knowledge spaces (See  Example 4 ). The BLIM model applied to FG or BG structures presents unidentifiability issues, and the characteristics of the skill maps delineating FG and BG structures was given in  Spoto and Stefanutti (2020) . Since fuzzy skill maps generalize classical skill maps, as an application, the corresponding probabilistic framework for fuzzy skills is introduced and the unidentifiability of CBLIM with fuzzy skills is discussed at last.

The paper is organized as follows. Section  2  provides a brief overview of knowledge space theory and fuzzy set theory. Basic concepts about fuzzy skill maps are introduced. In Section  3 , we explore the necessary and sufficient conditions for delineating FG and BG knowledge structures from fuzzy skill maps and we also discuss their relation to the theory presented in  Spoto and Stefanutti (2020) . Section  4  introduces the probabilistic framework to fuzzy skill maps and discusses the unidentifiability of CBLIM with fuzzy skills. Finally, in Section  5 , we provide a summary of the main results of our study.

In the classical case, the conjunctive and disjunctive models are two important models for delineating knowledge structures by a skill map. For the conjunctive model, solving the item  
                         q

A simple example in real world may help clarify the new definition introduced about fuzzy skill maps.

Example 2 
                         Let the knowledge domain  
                               Q 
                             be “Addition and subtraction of fractions”. For this knowledge domain,  Stefanutti and de Chiusole (2017)  built a dichotomous skill function for delineating the knowledge structure. The fuzzy skills are in  Table 3 . Items and the fuzzy skill map are in  Table 4 , where LCM is “Least Common Multiple” and GCD is “Greatest Common Divisor” for short. Fuzzy skills can be seen as the division of a skill into different levels through the threshold. For instance, Skill  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             (Convert different denominator to the same denominator.) is divided into three levels. The first level is  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  
                                     
                                        s 
                                     
                                     
                                        3 
                                     
                                  
                                  , 
                                  0 
                                  . 
                                  6 
                                  ) 
                               
                            , and an individual can convert different denominators in the item something like “ 
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                  
                                  : 
                                  
                                     
                                        5 
                                     
                                     
                                        6 
                                     
                                  
                                  + 
                                  
                                     
                                        5 
                                     
                                     
                                        12 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            ” to the same denominator, when his skill  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             has a proficiency of not less than 0.6. It means “when the LCM of denominators is equal to one of them”, an individual with  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             proficiency of no less than 0.6 can “Convert different denominators to the same denominator”. The second level is  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  
                                     
                                        s 
                                     
                                     
                                        3 
                                     
                                  
                                  , 
                                  0 
                                  . 
                                  8 
                                  ) 
                               
                            , and an individual can convert different denominators in the item something like “ 
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        5 
                                     
                                  
                                  : 
                                  
                                     
                                        5 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                  
                                  − 
                                  
                                     
                                        8 
                                     
                                     
                                        13 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            ” to the same denominator, when his skill  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             has a proficiency of not less than 0.8. It means “when the LCM of denominators is equal to the product of them”, an individual with  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             proficiency of no less than 0.8 can “Convert different denominators to the same denominator”. The highest level is  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  
                                     
                                        s 
                                     
                                     
                                        3 
                                     
                                  
                                  , 
                                  1 
                                  ) 
                               
                            . When an individual’s skill  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             has a proficiency 1, he can convert different denominators in any item to the same denominator. It means he fully mastered the skill  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                            . In this example, it is easy to check that  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             is a specific upper fuzzy skill for  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        3 
                                     
                                  
                                  : 
                                  
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                     
                                        15 
                                     
                                  
                                  − 
                                  
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                     
                                        20 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            . It means only item  
                               
                                  
                                     q 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             needs the skill  
                               
                                  
                                     s 
                                  
                                  
                                     3 
                                  
                               
                             with the highest proficiency of “Convert different denominator to the same denominator”, “when the LCM of denominators is a strict multiple of each of them”.

Theorem 1  and  Theorem 2  establish necessary and sufficient conditions for having a backward-graded closure space and a forward-graded knowledge space respectively. The next theorem establishes necessary and sufficient conditions for having a forward-graded closure space. For that, we need the following definitions and theorem, and the following paragraph and  Theorem 3  can be found in  Sun et al. (2021) .

In this section, we consider the unidentifiability of CBLIM as an application of BG and FG knowledge structures from fuzzy skill maps. First of all, we need associate fuzzy skills with the probabilistic framework. A knowledge state represents the subset of items from the considered domain  
                         Q 
                       that an individual masters. However, in a real world, an individual masters the item but could not solve it in case of a careless error. On the other hand, an individual could not master the item but solve it in case of a lucky guess. It means that the response pattern may be not consistent with the latent state due to the error probabilities. Let  
                         
                            R 
                            = 
                            
                               
                                  2 
                               
                               
                                  Q 
                               
                            
                         
                       denote the set of all possible response patterns  
                         R 
                       on the domain  
                         Q 
                      . Thus,  Falmagne and Doignon (1988)  introduced a probabilistic framework in KST. A probabilistic knowledge structure is defined as a triple  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            K 
                            , 
                            π 
                            ) 
                         
                      , where  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            K 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a knowledge structure and  
                         π 
                       is a probability distribution on  
                         K 
                      . Denote  
                         
                            P 
                            
                               ( 
                               R 
                               ∣ 
                               K 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       the conditional probabilities for all  
                         
                            R 
                            ∈ 
                            R 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            K 
                            ∈ 
                            K 
                         
                      . And the marginal distribution on  
                         R 
                       is predicted by  
                         
                            
                               
                                  P 
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     R 
                                     ) 
                                  
                                  = 
                                  
                                     
                                        ∑

                                        ∈ 
                                        K 
                                     
                                  
                                  P

                                     R 
                                     ∣ 
                                     K 
                                     ) 
                                  
                                  π 
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     K 
                                     ) 
                                  
                                  .

                         This example allows us to naturally introduce fuzzy skills into the BLIM model. Fuzzy skills can be utilized to create a flexible model. The extension of BLIM enables estimation of the ratio of each fuzzy skill equivalence class. For a given knowledge state  
                               K

                               K 
                             can give a more detailed classification of strategies in this extension model.

Proposition 2 
                         
                            The following assertions are equivalent. 
                         
                         
                            (i). The function  
                            
                               g 
                             
                            is locally one-to-one at some point in  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     Θ 
                                  
                                  
                                     F 
                                  
                               
                            
                            ;

                               p 
                             
                            is one-to-one; 
                         
                         
                            (iii). The function  
                            
                               g 
                             
                            is one-to-one.

The following assertions are equivalent.

(i). The function  
                            
                               g 
                             
                            is locally one-to-one at some point in  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     Θ 
                                  
                                  
                                     F 
                                  
                               
                            
                            ;

(ii). The problem function  
                            
                               p 
                             
                            is one-to-one;

(iii). The function  
                            
                               g 
                             
                            is one-to-one.

Remark 6 
                         The proof of this proposition can be referred to the proof of Proposition 7 in  Heller et al. (2015) . We find that the proof in the fuzzy case is essentially the same as the one that  Heller et al. (2015)  provided for the dichotomous case. Proposition 2 shows that  
                               g 
                             cannot be locally one-to-one at any point without  
                               p 
                             being one-to-one. The latter, however, provides that  
                               g 
                             is one-to-one. This leads to the situation that  
                               g 
                             is one-to-one if and only if it is locally one-to-one at some point, a very special situation indeed. This proposition is similar to the dichotomous case in  Heller et al. (2015) . 
                         It is obvious to see the following corollary.

The proof of this proposition can be referred to the proof of Proposition 7 in  Heller et al. (2015) . We find that the proof in the fuzzy case is essentially the same as the one that  Heller et al. (2015)  provided for the dichotomous case. Proposition 2 shows that  
                               g 
                             cannot be locally one-to-one at any point without  
                               p 
                             being one-to-one. The latter, however, provides that  
                               g 
                             is one-to-one. This leads to the situation that  
                               g 
                             is one-to-one if and only if it is locally one-to-one at some point, a very special situation indeed. This proposition is similar to the dichotomous case in  Heller et al. (2015) .

It is obvious to see the following corollary.

Proposition 3

                            , then the conjunctive (disjunctive) CBLIM with the fuzzy skill map is unidentifiable.

If a fuzzy skill map has a specific upper (lower) fuzzy skill for an item  
                            
                               
                                  q 
                                  ∈ 
                                  Q 
                               
                            
                            , then the conjunctive (disjunctive) CBLIM with the fuzzy skill map is unidentifiable.

The paper establishes necessary and sufficient conditions for fuzzy skill maps to delineate a BG simple closure space, a FG knowledge space, and a FG simple closure space. In contrast to specific skills in skill maps, specific upper and lower fuzzy skills, introduced in Section  3 , play a crucial role in fuzzy skill maps. We find that a fuzzy skill map has specific upper fuzzy skills for item  
                         q 
                       if and only if the simple closure space delineated via the conjunctive model by the fuzzy skill map is backward-graded in item  
                         q 
                      . Similarly, a fuzzy skill map has specific lower fuzzy skills for item  
                         q 
                       if and only if the knowledge space delineated via the disjunctive model by a fuzzy skill map is forward-graded for item  
                         q 
                      . On the other hand,  Theorem 4  establishes necessary and sufficient conditions for having a forward-graded closure space. However, conditions (i) and (ii) stated in  Theorem 4  do not necessarily guarantee a BG knowledge space, as demonstrated in  Example 4 . Although the fuzzy skill map fulfills conditions (i) and (ii), the delineated knowledge space  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               d 
                            
                            
                               τ 
                            
                         
                       does not exhibit backward-graded characteristics. One reason for this is that the knowledge structures delineated via conjunctive and disjunctive models by a fuzzy skill map are not necessarily dual, unlike the dichotomous case. This also demonstrates that the generalization of classical conclusions to the fuzzy case is not a simple matter of generalization. Hence, establishing necessary and sufficient conditions for the BG knowledge space is an important issue for our future research. Finally, as an application, we explore the relationship between fuzzy skills and the theory of probability knowledge structures. We find that the CBLIM with fuzzy skill maps, containing specific upper and lower fuzzy skills, is unidentifiable.

Just like classical skill multimaps, the fuzzy skill multimap also includes a corresponding competency model ( Sun et al., 2021 ). In future research, it is important to identify broader conditions for delineating FG or BG knowledge structures via the competency model of fuzzy skill multimaps. Based on our application in this study, the unidentifiability of the CBLIM with a fuzzy skill map relies on the unidentifiability of the BLIM induced by the CBLIM. The BLIM model applied to FG or BG structures presents unidentifiability issues, while they are not the sole cases. In this regard, defining a fuzzy skill multimap that delineates unidentifiable knowledge structures is another challenge for further investigation.

Lastly, the most important challenge for future research is the empirical indistinguishability ( Stefanutti & Spoto, 2021 ) of CBLIM and fuzzy skill.  Spoto and Stefanutti (2022)  explore the empirical indistinguishability of a skill map. The unidentifiability issue typically arises when two sets of model parameters result in the same probability distribution for the response patterns. These parameter sets are applied to the same knowledge structure. The unidentifiability of CBLIM with fuzzy skill is obtained relatively easily in this paper. Empirical indistinguishability is a stronger form of unidentifiability, involving not only the parameters but also the structural and combinatorial properties of the model. In contrast to the unidentifiability of CBLIM with fuzzy skill, empirical indistinguishability represents a significantly more complex and crucial issue.

The fuzzy approach can be a good description of the fact that expertise is acquired through incremental improvements and mastery of increasingly complex tasks. Fuzzy skill proficiency embraces the idea of skill development as a continuous process, allowing individuals to approach their skill development in a incremental manner. However, the negative aspects of the fuzzy approach cannot be ignored. There are more equivalence classes compared to the number of  
                         
                            
                               2 
                            
                            
                               S 
                            
                         
                      . Although this would allow for a more detailed delineation of the strategies used to delineate the same knowledge state, it would make the problems arising from the fact that the problem function is not injective more obvious. The fuzzy approach requires more parameters compared to classical skill maps. And determining the proficiency on a skill is also an issue that needs to be taken seriously.
